{""name"":""conn"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_conn:\n\nconn\n----\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - This is the time of the first packet.\n\n   * - ``uid`` (string)\n     - A unique identifier of the connection.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The originator's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The originator's port number.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The responder's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The responder's port number.\n\n   * - ``proto`` (string - enum)\n     - The transport layer protocol of the connection.\n\n   * - ``service`` (string)\n     - An identification of an application protocol being sent over\n       the connection.\n\n   * - ``duration`` (number - interval)\n     - How long the connection lasted.  For 3-way or 4-way connection\n       tear-downs, this will not include the final ACK.\n\n   * - ``orig_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of payload bytes the originator sent. For TCP\n       this is taken from sequence numbers and might be inaccurate\n       (e.g., due to large connections).\n\n   * - ``resp_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of payload bytes the responder sent. See\n       *orig_bytes*.\n\n   * - ``conn_state`` (string)\n     - Possible *conn_state* values:\n       \n       * S0: Connection attempt seen, no reply.\n       \n       * S1: Connection established, not terminated.\n       \n       * SF: Normal establishment and termination.\n         Note that this is the same symbol as for state S1.\n         You can tell the two apart because for S1 there will not be any\n         byte counts in the summary, while for SF there will be.\n       \n       * REJ: Connection attempt rejected.\n       \n       * S2: Connection established and close attempt by originator seen\n         (but no reply from responder).\n       \n       * S3: Connection established and close attempt by responder seen\n         (but no reply from originator).\n       \n       * RSTO: Connection established, originator aborted (sent a RST).\n       \n       * RSTR: Responder sent a RST.\n       \n       * RSTOS0: Originator sent a SYN followed by a RST, we never saw a\n         SYN-ACK from the responder.\n       \n       * RSTRH: Responder sent a SYN ACK followed by a RST, we never saw a\n         SYN from the (purported) originator.\n       \n       * SH: Originator sent a SYN followed by a FIN, we never saw a\n         SYN ACK from the responder (hence the connection was \""half\"" open).\n       \n       * SHR: Responder sent a SYN ACK followed by a FIN, we never saw a\n         SYN from the originator.\n       \n       * OTH: No SYN seen, just midstream traffic (one example of this\n         is a \""partial connection\"" that was not later closed).\n\n   * - ``local_orig`` (boolean - bool)\n     - If the connection is originated locally, this value will be T.\n       If it was originated remotely it will be F.  In the case that\n       the `Site::local_nets` variable is undefined, this\n       field will be left empty at all times.\n\n   * - ``local_resp`` (boolean - bool)\n     - If the connection is responded to locally, this value will be T.\n       If it was responded to remotely it will be F.  In the case that\n       the `Site::local_nets` variable is undefined, this\n       field will be left empty at all times.\n\n   * - ``missed_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Indicates the number of bytes missed in content gaps, which\n       is representative of packet loss.  A value other than zero\n       will normally cause protocol analysis to fail but some\n       analysis may have been completed prior to the packet loss.\n\n   * - ``history`` (string)\n     - Records the state history of connections as a string of\n       letters.  The meaning of those letters is:\n       \n       \n       * s: a SYN w/o the ACK bit set\n       * h: a SYN+ACK (\""handshake\"")\n       * a: a pure ACK\n       * d: packet with payload (\""data\"")\n       * f: packet with FIN bit set\n       * r: packet with RST bit set\n       * c: packet with a bad checksum (applies to UDP too)\n       * g: a content gap\n       * t: packet with retransmitted payload\n       * w: packet with a zero window advertisement\n       * i: inconsistent packet (e.g. FIN+RST bits set)\n       * q: multi-flag packet (SYN+FIN or SYN+RST bits set)\n       * ^: connection direction was flipped by Zeek's heuristic\n       \n       \n       If the event comes from the originator, the letter is in\n       upper-case; if it comes from the responder, it's in\n       lower-case.  The 'a', 'd', 'i' and 'q' flags are\n       recorded a maximum of one time in either direction regardless\n       of how many are actually seen.  'f', 'h', 'r' and\n       's' can be recorded multiple times for either direction\n       if the associated sequence number differs from the\n       last-seen packet of the same flag type.\n       'c', 'g', 't' and 'w' are recorded in a logarithmic fashion:\n       the second instance represents that the event was seen\n       (at least) 10 times; the third instance, 100 times; etc.\n\n   * - ``orig_pkts`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of packets that the originator sent.\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``orig_ip_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of IP level bytes that the originator sent (as seen on\n       the wire, taken from the IP total_length header field).\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``resp_pkts`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of packets that the responder sent.\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``resp_ip_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of IP level bytes that the responder sent (as seen on\n       the wire, taken from the IP total_length header field).\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``tunnel_parents`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - If this connection was over a tunnel, indicate the\n       *uid* values for any encapsulating parent connections\n       used over the lifetime of this inner connection.\n\n   * - ``orig_cc`` (string)\n     - The name of the node where this connection was analyzed.\n       Country code for GeoIP lookup of the originating IP address.\n\n   * - ``resp_cc`` (string)\n     - Country code for GeoIP lookup of the responding IP address.\n\n   * - ``suri_ids`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - The suri_ids information.\n\n   * - ``spcap.url`` (string)\n     - The spcap.url information.\n\n   * - ``spcap.rule`` (integer - count)\n     - The spcap.rule information.\n\n   * - ``spcap.trigger`` (string)\n     - The spcap.trigger information.\n\n   * - ``app`` (array[string] - vector of string)\n     - The app information.\n\n   * - ``corelight_shunted`` (boolean - bool)\n     - The corelight_shunted information.\n\n   * - ``orig_shunted_pkts`` (integer - count)\n     - The orig_shunted_pkts information.\n\n   * - ``orig_shunted_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The orig_shunted_bytes information.\n\n   * - ``resp_shunted_pkts`` (integer - count)\n     - The resp_shunted_pkts information.\n\n   * - ``resp_shunted_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The resp_shunted_bytes information.\n\n   * - ``orig_l2_addr`` (string)\n     - Link-layer address of the originator, if available.\n\n   * - ``resp_l2_addr`` (string)\n     - Link-layer address of the responder, if available.\n\n   * - ``id_orig_h_n.src`` (string)\n     - How we determined the name/address pair. Either\n       ``DNS_A`` representing the DNS_A* family of query types,\n       or ``DNS_PTR`` for reverse DNS lookups.\n\n   * - ``id_orig_h_n.vals`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - The set of names we observed for a given address.\n\n   * - ``id_resp_h_n.src`` (string)\n     - How we determined the name/address pair. Either\n       ``DNS_A`` representing the DNS_A* family of query types,\n       or ``DNS_PTR`` for reverse DNS lookups.\n\n   * - ``id_resp_h_n.vals`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - The set of names we observed for a given address.\n\n   * - ``vlan`` (integer - int)\n     - The outer VLAN for this connection, if applicable.\n\n   * - ``inner_vlan`` (integer - int)\n     - The inner VLAN for this connection, if applicable.\n\n   * - ``community_id`` (string)\n     - The community_id information.\n"",""schema"":"{\n  \""$schema\"": \""http://json-schema.org/draft-07/schema#\"",\n {""name"":""conn_long"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_conn_long:\n\nconn_long\n---------\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - This is the time of the first packet.\n\n   * - ``uid`` (string)\n     - A unique identifier of the connection.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The originator's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The originator's port number.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The responder's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The responder's port number.\n\n   * - ``proto`` (string - enum)\n     - The transport layer protocol of the connection.\n\n   * - ``service`` (string)\n     - An identification of an application protocol being sent over\n       the connection.\n\n   * - ``duration`` (number - interval)\n     - How long the connection lasted.  For 3-way or 4-way connection\n       tear-downs, this will not include the final ACK.\n\n   * - ``orig_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of payload bytes the originator sent. For TCP\n       this is taken from sequence numbers and might be inaccurate\n       (e.g., due to large connections).\n\n   * - ``resp_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of payload bytes the responder sent. See\n       *orig_bytes*.\n\n   * - ``conn_state`` (string)\n     - Possible *conn_state* values:\n       \n       * S0: Connection attempt seen, no reply.\n       \n       * S1: Connection established, not terminated.\n       \n       * SF: Normal establishment and termination.\n         Note that this is the same symbol as for state S1.\n         You can tell the two apart because for S1 there will not be any\n         byte counts in the summary, while for SF there will be.\n       \n       * REJ: Connection attempt rejected.\n       \n       * S2: Connection established and close attempt by originator seen\n         (but no reply from responder).\n       \n       * S3: Connection established and close attempt by responder seen\n         (but no reply from originator).\n       \n       * RSTO: Connection established, originator aborted (sent a RST).\n       \n       * RSTR: Responder sent a RST.\n       \n       * RSTOS0: Originator sent a SYN followed by a RST, we never saw a\n         SYN-ACK from the responder.\n       \n       * RSTRH: Responder sent a SYN ACK followed by a RST, we never saw a\n         SYN from the (purported) originator.\n       \n       * SH: Originator sent a SYN followed by a FIN, we never saw a\n         SYN ACK from the responder (hence the connection was \""half\"" open).\n       \n       * SHR: Responder sent a SYN ACK followed by a FIN, we never saw a\n         SYN from the originator.\n       \n       * OTH: No SYN seen, just midstream traffic (one example of this\n         is a \""partial connection\"" that was not later closed).\n\n   * - ``local_orig`` (boolean - bool)\n     - If the connection is originated locally, this value will be T.\n       If it was originated remotely it will be F.  In the case that\n       the `Site::local_nets` variable is undefined, this\n       field will be left empty at all times.\n\n   * - ``local_resp`` (boolean - bool)\n     - If the connection is responded to locally, this value will be T.\n       If it was responded to remotely it will be F.  In the case that\n       the `Site::local_nets` variable is undefined, this\n       field will be left empty at all times.\n\n   * - ``missed_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Indicates the number of bytes missed in content gaps, which\n       is representative of packet loss.  A value other than zero\n       will normally cause protocol analysis to fail but some\n       analysis may have been completed prior to the packet loss.\n\n   * - ``history`` (string)\n     - Records the state history of connections as a string of\n       letters.  The meaning of those letters is:\n       \n       \n       * s: a SYN w/o the ACK bit set\n       * h: a SYN+ACK (\""handshake\"")\n       * a: a pure ACK\n       * d: packet with payload (\""data\"")\n       * f: packet with FIN bit set\n       * r: packet with RST bit set\n       * c: packet with a bad checksum (applies to UDP too)\n       * g: a content gap\n       * t: packet with retransmitted payload\n       * w: packet with a zero window advertisement\n       * i: inconsistent packet (e.g. FIN+RST bits set)\n       * q: multi-flag packet (SYN+FIN or SYN+RST bits set)\n       * ^: connection direction was flipped by Zeek's heuristic\n       \n       \n       If the event comes from the originator, the letter is in\n       upper-case; if it comes from the responder, it's in\n       lower-case.  The 'a', 'd', 'i' and 'q' flags are\n       recorded a maximum of one time in either direction regardless\n       of how many are actually seen.  'f', 'h', 'r' and\n       's' can be recorded multiple times for either direction\n       if the associated sequence number differs from the\n       last-seen packet of the same flag type.\n       'c', 'g', 't' and 'w' are recorded in a logarithmic fashion:\n       the second instance represents that the event was seen\n       (at least) 10 times; the third instance, 100 times; etc.\n\n   * - ``orig_pkts`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of packets that the originator sent.\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``orig_ip_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of IP level bytes that the originator sent (as seen on\n       the wire, taken from the IP total_length header field).\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``resp_pkts`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of packets that the responder sent.\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``resp_ip_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of IP level bytes that the responder sent (as seen on\n       the wire, taken from the IP total_length header field).\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``tunnel_parents`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - If this connection was over a tunnel, indicate the\n       *uid* values for any encapsulating parent connections\n       used over the lifetime of this inner connection.\n\n   * - ``orig_cc`` (string)\n     - The name of the node where this connection was analyzed.\n       Country code for GeoIP lookup of the originating IP address.\n\n   * - ``resp_cc`` (string)\n     - Country code for GeoIP lookup of the responding IP address.\n\n   * - ``suri_ids`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - The suri_ids information.\n\n   * - ``spcap.url`` (string)\n     - The spcap.url information.\n\n   * - ``spcap.rule`` (integer - count)\n     - The spcap.rule information.\n\n   * - ``spcap.trigger`` (string)\n     - The spcap.trigger information.\n\n   * - ``app`` (array[string] - vector of string)\n     - The app information.\n\n   * - ``corelight_shunted`` (boolean - bool)\n     - The corelight_shunted information.\n\n   * - ``orig_shunted_pkts`` (integer - count)\n     - The orig_shunted_pkts information.\n\n   * - ``orig_shunted_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The orig_shunted_bytes information.\n\n   * - ``resp_shunted_pkts`` (integer - count)\n     - The resp_shunted_pkts information.\n\n   * - ``resp_shunted_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The resp_shunted_bytes information.\n\n   * - ``orig_l2_addr`` (string)\n     - Link-layer address of the originator, if available.\n\n   * - ``resp_l2_addr`` (string)\n     - Link-layer address of the responder, if available.\n\n   * - ``id_orig_h_n.src`` (string)\n     - How we determined the name/address pair. Either\n       ``DNS_A`` representing the DNS_A* family of query types,\n       or ``DNS_PTR`` for reverse DNS lookups.\n\n   * - ``id_orig_h_n.vals`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - The set of names we observed for a given address.\n\n   * - ``id_resp_h_n.src`` (string)\n     - How we determined the name/address pair. {""name"":""conn_red"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_conn_red:\n\nconn_red\n--------\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - This is the time of the first packet.\n\n   * - ``uid`` (string)\n     - A unique identifier of the connection.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The originator's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The originator's port number.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The responder's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The responder's port number.\n\n   * - ``proto`` (string - enum)\n     - The transport layer protocol of the connection.\n\n   * - ``service`` (string)\n     - An identification of an application protocol being sent over\n       the connection.\n\n   * - ``duration`` (number - interval)\n     - How long the connection lasted.  For 3-way or 4-way connection\n       tear-downs, this will not include the final ACK.\n\n   * - ``orig_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of payload bytes the originator sent. For TCP\n       this is taken from sequence numbers and might be inaccurate\n       (e.g., due to large connections).\n\n   * - ``resp_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of payload bytes the responder sent. See\n       *orig_bytes*.\n\n   * - ``conn_state`` (string)\n     - Possible *conn_state* values:\n       \n       * S0: Connection attempt seen, no reply.\n       \n       * S1: Connection established, not terminated.\n       \n       * SF: Normal establishment and termination.\n         Note that this is the same symbol as for state S1.\n         You can tell the two apart because for S1 there will not be any\n         byte counts in the summary, while for SF there will be.\n       \n       * REJ: Connection attempt rejected.\n       \n       * S2: Connection established and close attempt by originator seen\n         (but no reply from responder).\n       \n       * S3: Connection established and close attempt by responder seen\n         (but no reply from originator).\n       \n       * RSTO: Connection established, originator aborted (sent a RST).\n       \n       * RSTR: Responder sent a RST.\n       \n       * RSTOS0: Originator sent a SYN followed by a RST, we never saw a\n         SYN-ACK from the responder.\n       \n       * RSTRH: Responder sent a SYN ACK followed by a RST, we never saw a\n         SYN from the (purported) originator.\n       \n       * SH: Originator sent a SYN followed by a FIN, we never saw a\n         SYN ACK from the responder (hence the connection was \""half\"" open).\n       \n       * SHR: Responder sent a SYN ACK followed by a FIN, we never saw a\n         SYN from the originator.\n       \n       * OTH: No SYN seen, just midstream traffic (one example of this\n         is a \""partial connection\"" that was not later closed).\n\n   * - ``local_orig`` (boolean - bool)\n     - If the connection is originated locally, this value will be T.\n       If it was originated remotely it will be F.  In the case that\n       the `Site::local_nets` variable is undefined, this\n       field will be left empty at all times.\n\n   * - ``local_resp`` (boolean - bool)\n     - If the connection is responded to locally, this value will be T.\n       If it was responded to remotely it will be F.  In the case that\n       the `Site::local_nets` variable is undefined, this\n       field will be left empty at all times.\n\n   * - ``missed_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Indicates the number of bytes missed in content gaps, which\n       is representative of packet loss.  A value other than zero\n       will normally cause protocol analysis to fail but some\n       analysis may have been completed prior to the packet loss.\n\n   * - ``history`` (string)\n     - Records the state history of connections as a string of\n       letters.  The meaning of those letters is:\n       \n       \n       * s: a SYN w/o the ACK bit set\n       * h: a SYN+ACK (\""handshake\"")\n       * a: a pure ACK\n       * d: packet with payload (\""data\"")\n       * f: packet with FIN bit set\n       * r: packet with RST bit set\n       * c: packet with a bad checksum (applies to UDP too)\n       * g: a content gap\n       * t: packet with retransmitted payload\n       * w: packet with a zero window advertisement\n       * i: inconsistent packet (e.g. FIN+RST bits set)\n       * q: multi-flag packet (SYN+FIN or SYN+RST bits set)\n       * ^: connection direction was flipped by Zeek's heuristic\n       \n       \n       If the event comes from the originator, the letter is in\n       upper-case; if it comes from the responder, it's in\n       lower-case.  The 'a', 'd', 'i' and 'q' flags are\n       recorded a maximum of one time in either direction regardless\n       of how many are actually seen.  'f', 'h', 'r' and\n       's' can be recorded multiple times for either direction\n       if the associated sequence number differs from the\n       last-seen packet of the same flag type.\n       'c', 'g', 't' and 'w' are recorded in a logarithmic fashion:\n       the second instance represents that the event was seen\n       (at least) 10 times; the third instance, 100 times; etc.\n\n   * - ``orig_pkts`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of packets that the originator sent.\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``orig_ip_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of IP level bytes that the originator sent (as seen on\n       the wire, taken from the IP total_length header field).\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``resp_pkts`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of packets that the responder sent.\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - ``resp_ip_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of IP level bytes that the responder sent (as seen on\n       the wire, taken from the IP total_length header field).\n       Only set if `use_conn_size_analyzer` = T.\n\n   * - {""name"":""dns"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_dns:\n\ndns\n---\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - The earliest time at which a DNS protocol message over the\n       associated connection is observed.\n\n   * - ``uid`` (string)\n     - A unique identifier of the connection over which DNS messages\n       are being transferred.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The originator's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The originator's port number.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The responder's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The responder's port number.\n\n   * - ``proto`` (string - enum)\n     - The transport layer protocol of the connection.\n\n   * - ``trans_id`` (integer - count)\n     - A 16-bit identifier assigned by the program that generated\n       the DNS query.  Also used in responses to match up replies to\n       outstanding queries.\n\n   * - ``rtt`` (number - interval)\n     - Round trip time for the query and response. This indicates\n       the delay between when the request was seen until the\n       answer started.\n\n   * - ``query`` (string)\n     - The domain name that is the subject of the DNS query.\n\n   * - ``qclass`` (integer - count)\n     - The QCLASS value specifying the class of the query.\n\n   * - ``qclass_name`` (string)\n     - A descriptive name for the class of the query.\n\n   * - ``qtype`` count)\n     - The response code value in DNS response messages.\n\n   * - ``rcode_name`` (string)\n     - A descriptive name for the response code value.\n\n   * - ``AA`` (boolean - bool)\n     - The Authoritative Answer bit for response messages specifies\n       that the responding name server is an authority for the\n       domain name in the question section.\n\n   * - ``TC`` (boolean - bool)\n     - The Truncation bit specifies that the message was truncated.\n\n   * - ``RD`` (boolean - bool)\n     - The Recursion Desired bit in a request message indicates that\n       the client wants recursive service for this query.\n\n   * - ``RA`` (boolean - bool)\n     - The Recursion Available bit in a response message indicates\n       that the name server supports recursive queries.\n\n   * - ``Z`` (integer - count)\n     - A reserved field that is usually zero in\n       queries and responses.\n\n   * - ``answers`` (array[string] - vector of string)\n     - The set of resource descriptions in the query answer.\n\n   * - ``TTLs`` (array[number] - vector of interval)\n     - The caching intervals of the associated RRs described by the\n       *answers* field.\n\n   * {""name"":""notice"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_notice:\n\nnotice\n------\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - An absolute time indicating when the notice occurred,\n       defaults to the current network time.\n\n   * - ``uid`` (string)\n     - A connection UID which uniquely identifies the endpoints\n       concerned with the notice.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The originator's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The originator's port number.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The responder's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The responder's port number.\n\n   * - ``fuid`` (string)\n     - A file unique ID if this notice is related to a file.  If\n       the *f* field is provided, this will be automatically filled\n       out.\n\n   * - ``file_mime_type`` (string)\n     - A mime type if the notice is related to a file.  If the *f*\n       field is provided, this will be automatically filled out.\n\n   * - ``file_desc`` (string)\n     - Frequently files can be \""described\"" to give a bit more\n       context.  This field will typically be automatically filled\n       out from an fa_file record.  For example, if a notice was\n       related to a file over HTTP, the URL of the request would\n       be shown.\n\n   * - ``proto`` (string - enum)\n     - The transport protocol. Filled automatically when either\n       *conn*, *iconn* or *p* is specified.\n\n   * - ``note`` (string - enum)\n     - The `Notice::Type` of the notice.\n\n   * - ``msg`` (string)\n     - The human readable message for the notice.\n\n   * - ``sub`` (string)\n     - The human readable sub-message.\n\n   * - ``src`` (string - addr)\n     - Source address, if we don't have a `conn_id`.\n\n   * - ``dst`` (string - addr)\n     - Destination address.\n\n   * - ``p`` (integer - port)\n     - Associated port, if we don't have a `conn_id`.\n\n   * - ``n`` (integer - count)\n     - Associated count, or perhaps a status code.\n\n   * - ``peer_descr`` (string)\n     - Textual description for the peer that raised this notice,\n       including name, host address and port.\n\n   * - ``actions`` unique notice should be suppressed.\n\n   * - ``remote_location.country_code`` (string)\n     - The country code.\n\n   * - ``remote_location.region`` (string)\n     - The region.\n\n   * - ``remote_location.city`` (string)\n     - The city.\n\n   * - ``remote_location.latitude`` (number - double)\n     - Latitude.\n\n   * - ``remote_location.longitude`` (number - double)\n     - {""name"":""files"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_files:\n\nfiles\n-----\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - The time when the file was first seen.\n\n   * - ``fuid`` (string)\n     - An identifier associated with a single file.\n\n   * - ``tx_hosts`` (array[string] - set[addr])\n     - If this file was transferred over a network\n       connection this should show the host or hosts that\n       the data sourced from.\n\n   * - ``rx_hosts`` (array[string] - set[addr])\n     - If this file was transferred over a network\n       connection this should show the host or hosts that\n       the data traveled to.\n\n   * - ``conn_uids`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - Connection UIDs over which the file was transferred.\n\n   * - ``source`` (string)\n     - An identification of the source of the file data.  E.g. it\n       may be a network protocol over which it was transferred, or a\n       local file path which was read, or some other input source.\n\n   * - ``depth`` (integer - count)\n     - A value to represent the depth of this file in relation\n       to its source.  In SMTP, it is the depth of the MIME\n       attachment on the message.  In HTTP, it is the depth of the\n       request within the TCP connection.\n\n   * - ``analyzers`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - A set of analysis types done during the file analysis.\n\n   * - ``mime_type`` (string)\n     - A mime type provided by the strongest file magic signature\n       match against the *bof_buffer* field of `fa_file`,\n       or in the cases where no buffering of the beginning of file\n       occurs, an initial guess of the mime type based on the first\n       data seen.\n\n   * - ``filename`` (string)\n     - A filename for the file if one is available from the source\n       for the file.  These will frequently come from\n       \""Content-Disposition\"" headers in network protocols.\n\n   * - ``duration`` (number - interval)\n     - The duration the file was analyzed for.\n\n   * - ``local_orig`` (boolean - bool)\n     - If the source of this file is a network connection, this field\n       indicates if the data originated from the local network or not as\n       determined by the configured `Site::local_nets`.\n\n   * - ``is_orig`` (boolean - bool)\n     - If the source of this file is a network connection, this field\n       indicates if the file is being sent by the originator of the\n       connection or the responder.\n\n   * - ``seen_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of bytes provided to the file analysis engine for the file.\n\n   * - ``total_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - Total number of bytes that are supposed to comprise the full file.\n\n   * - ``missing_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of bytes in the file stream that were completely missed\n       during the process of analysis e.g. due to dropped packets.\n\n   * - ``overflow_bytes`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of bytes in the file stream that were not delivered to\n       stream file analyzers.  This could be overlapping bytes or\n       bytes that couldn't be reassembled.\n\n   * - ``timedout`` (boolean - bool)\n     - Whether the file analysis timed out at least once for the file.\n\n   * - ``parent_fuid`` (string)\n     - Identifier associated with a container file from which this one was\n       extracted as part of the file analysis.\n\n   * - ``md5`` (string)\n     - An MD5 digest of the file contents.\n\n   * - ``sha1`` (string)\n     - A SHA1 digest of the file contents.\n\n   * - ``sha256`` (string)\n     - A SHA256 digest of the file contents.\n\n   * - ``extracted`` (string)\n     - Local filename of extracted file.\n\n   * - ``extracted_cutoff`` (boolean - bool)\n     - Set to true if the file being extracted was cut off\n       so the whole file was not {""name"":""http"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_http:\n\nhttp\n----\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - Timestamp for when the request happened.\n\n   * - ``uid`` (string)\n     - Unique ID for the connection.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The originator's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The originator's port number.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The responder's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The responder's port number.\n\n   * - ``trans_depth`` (integer - count)\n     - Represents the pipelined depth into the connection of this\n       request/response transaction.\n\n   * - ``method`` (string)\n     - Verb used in the HTTP request (GET, POST, HEAD, etc.).\n\n   * - ``host`` (string)\n     - Value of the HOST header.\n\n   * - ``uri`` (string)\n     - URI used in the request.\n\n   * - ``referrer`` (string)\n     - Value of the \""referer\"" header.  The comment is deliberately\n       misspelled like the standard declares, but the name used here\n       is \""referrer\"", spelled correctly.\n\n   * - ``version`` (string)\n     - Value of the version portion of the reply. If you require\n       message-level detail, consider the `http_request` and\n       `http_reply` events, which report each message's\n       version string.\n\n   * - ``user_agent`` (string)\n     - Value of the User-Agent header from the client.\n\n   * - ``origin`` (string)\n     - Value of the Origin header from the client.\n\n   * - ``request_body_len`` (integer - count)\n     - Actual uncompressed content size of the data transferred from\n       the client.\n\n   * - ``response_body_len`` (integer - count)\n     - Actual uncompressed content size of the data transferred from\n       the server.\n\n   * - ``status_code`` (integer - count)\n     - Status code returned by the server.\n\n   * - ``status_msg`` (string)\n     - Status message returned by the server.\n\n   * - ``info_code`` (integer - count)\n     - Last seen 1xx informational reply code returned by the server.\n\n   * - ``info_msg`` (string)\n     - Last seen 1xx informational reply message returned by the server.\n\n   * - ``tags`` (array[string] - set[enum])\n     - A set of indicators of various attributes discovered and\n       related to a particular request/response pair.\n\n   * - ``username`` (string)\n     - Username if basic-auth is performed for the request.\n\n   * - ``password`` (string)\n     - Password if basic-auth is performed for the request.\n\n   * - ``proxied`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - All of the headers that may indicate if the request was proxied.\n\n   * - ``orig_fuids`` (array[string] - vector of string)\n     - An ordered vector of file unique IDs.\n       Limited to `HTTP::max_files_orig` entries.\n\n   * - ``orig_filenames`` (array[string] - vector of string)\n     - An ordered vector of filenames from the client.\n       Limited to `HTTP::max_files_orig` entries.\n\n   * - ``orig_mime_types`` (array[string] - vector of string)\n     - An ordered vector of mime types.\n       Limited to `HTTP::max_files_orig` entries.\n\n   * - {""name"":""ssl"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_ssl:\n\nssl\n---\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - Time when the SSL connection was first detected.\n\n   * - ``uid`` (string)\n     - Unique ID for the connection.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The originator's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The originator's port number.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The responder's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The responder's port number.\n\n   * - ``version`` (string)\n     - SSL/TLS version that the server chose.\n\n   * - ``cipher`` (string)\n     - SSL/TLS cipher suite that the server chose.\n\n   * - ``curve`` (string)\n     - Elliptic curve the server chose when using ECDH/ECDHE.\n\n   * - ``server_name`` (string)\n     - Value of the Server Name Indicator SSL/TLS extension.  It\n       indicates the server name that the client was requesting.\n\n   * - ``resumed`` (boolean - bool)\n     - Flag to indicate if the session was resumed reusing\n       the key material exchanged in an earlier connection.\n\n   * - ``last_alert`` (string)\n     - Last alert that was seen during the connection.\n\n   * - ``next_protocol`` (string)\n     - Next protocol the server chose using the application layer\n       next protocol extension, if present.\n\n   * - ``established`` (boolean - bool)\n     - Flag to indicate if this ssl session has been established\n       successfully, or if it was aborted during the handshake.\n\n   * - ``ssl_history`` (string)\n     - {""name"":""ssh"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_ssh:\n\nssh\n---\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - Time when the SSH connection began.\n\n   * - ``uid`` (string)\n     - Unique ID for the connection.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The originator's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The originator's port number.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The responder's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The responder's port number.\n\n   * - ``version`` (integer - count)\n     - SSH major version (1, 2, or unset). The version can be unset if the\n       client and server version strings are unset, malformed or incompatible\n       so no common version can be extracted. If no version can be extracted\n       even though both client and server versions are set a weird\n       will be generated.\n\n   * - ``auth_success`` (boolean - bool)\n     - Authentication result (T=success, F=failure, unset=unknown)\n\n   * - ``auth_attempts`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of authentication attemps we observed. There's always\n       at least one, since some servers might support no authentication at all.\n       It's important to note that not all of these are failures, since\n       some servers require two-factor auth (e.g. password AND pubkey)\n\n   * - ``direction`` (string - enum)\n     - Direction of the connection. If the client was a local host\n       logging into an external host, this would be OUTBOUND. INBOUND\n       would be set for the opposite situation.\n\n   * - ``client`` (string)\n     - The client's version string\n\n   * - ``server`` (string)\n     - The server's version string\n\n   * - Only created during logging.\n\n   * - ``software`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - Software that offered the service.\n\n   * - ``app`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - Apps that offered the service.\n\n   * - ``num_conns`` (integer - count)\n     - Number of connections for which the service was observed.\n\n   * - ``annotations`` (array[string] - vector of string)\n     - Annotation {""name"":""dhcp"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_dhcp:\n\ndhcp\n----\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - The earliest time at which a DHCP message over the\n       associated connection is observed.\n\n   * - ``uids`` (array[string] - set[string])\n     - A series of unique identifiers of the connections over which\n       DHCP is occurring.  This behavior with multiple connections is\n       unique to DHCP because of the way it uses broadcast packets\n       on local networks.\n\n   * - ``client_addr`` (string - addr)\n     - IP address of the client.  If a transaction\n       is only a client sending INFORM messages then\n       there is no lease information exchanged so this\n       is helpful to know who sent the messages.\n       Getting an address in this field does require\n       that the client sources at least one DHCP message\n       using a non-broadcast address.\n\n   * - ``server_addr`` (string - addr)\n     - IP address of the server involved in actually\n       handing out the lease. 81.\n\n   * - ``domain`` (string)\n     - Domain given by the server in option 15.\n\n   * - ``requested_addr`` (string - addr)\n     - IP address requested by the client.\n\n   * - ``assigned_addr`` {""name"":""stepping"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_stepping:\n\nstepping\n--------\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - {""name"":""ntp"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_ntp:\n\nntp\n---\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - Timestamp for when the event happened.\n\n   * - ``uid`` (string)\n     - Unique ID for the connection.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The originator's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The originator's port number.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The responder's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The responder's port number.\n\n   * - ``version`` (integer - count)\n     - The NTP version number (1, 2, 3, 4).\n\n   * - ``mode`` (integer - count)\n     - The NTP mode being used.\n\n   * - ``stratum`` (integer - count)\n     - The stratum (primary server, secondary server, etc.).\n\n   * - ``poll`` (number - interval)\n     - The maximum interval between successive messages.\n\n   * - ``precision`` (number - interval)\n     - The precision of the system clock.\n\n   * - ``root_delay`` (number - interval)\n     - Total round-trip delay to the reference clock.\n\n   * - ``root_disp`` (number - interval)\n     - Total dispersion to the reference clock.\n\n   * - ``ref_id`` (string)\n     - For stratum 0, 4 character string used for debugging.\n       For stratum 1, ID assigned to the reference clock by IANA.\n       Above stratum 1, when using IPv4, the IP address of the reference\n       clock.  Note that the NTP protocol did not originally specify a\n       large enough field to represent IPv6 addresses, so they use\n       the first four bytes of the MD5 hash of the reference clock's\n       IPv6 address (i.e. an IPv4 address here is not necessarily IPv4).\n\n   * - ``ref_time`` (time)\n     - Time when the system clock was last set or correct.\n\n   * - ``org_time`` (time)\n     - Time at the client when the request departed for the NTP server.\n\n   * - ``rec_time`` (time)\n     - Time at the server when the request arrived from the NTP client.\n\n   * - ``xmt_time`` (time)\n     - {""name"":""snmp"",""text"":"".. _ref_logs_snmp:\n\nsnmp\n----\n.. list-table::\n   :header-rows: 1\n   :class: longtable\n   :widths: 1 3\n\n   * - Field (Type)\n     - Description\n\n   * - ``ts`` (time)\n     - Timestamp of first packet belonging to the SNMP session.\n\n   * - ``uid`` (string)\n     - The unique ID for the connection.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The originator's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.orig_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The originator's port number.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_h`` (string - addr)\n     - The responder's IP address.\n\n   * - ``id.resp_p`` (integer - port)\n     - The responder's port number.\n\n   * - ``duration`` (number - interval)\n     - The amount of time between the first packet beloning to\n       the SNMP session and the latest one seen.\n\n   * - ``version`` (string)\n     - The version of SNMP being used.\n\n   * - ``community`` (string)\n     - The community string of the first SNMP packet associated with\n       the session.  This is used as part of SNMP's (v1 and v2c)\n       administrative/security framework.  See :rfc:`1157` or :rfc:`1901`.\n\n   * - ``get_requests`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of variable bindings in GetRequest/GetNextRequest PDUs\n       seen for the session.\n\n   * - ``get_bulk_requests`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of variable bindings in GetBulkRequest PDUs seen for\n       the session.\n\n   * - ``get_responses`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of variable bindings in GetResponse/Response PDUs seen\n       for the session.\n\n   * - ``set_requests`` (integer - count)\n     - The number of variable bindings in SetRequest PDUs seen for\n
